[]{#classcudaq_1_1scalar__callback .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[scalar_callback]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15scalar_callbackE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A callback wrapper that encapsulates a user-provided function taking
    a set of complex parameters and returning a complex result.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

    :   Constructs a scalar callback from a callable object.

        Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **Callable** -- The type of the callable object. It must
            satisfy the signature:
            std::complex\<double\>([`const`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre} std::unordered_map\<std::string,
            std::complex\<double\>\> &).

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **callable** -- The callable object to be wrapped and stored
            for later invocation.

    and sizes.

    The tuple elements are:

        .notranslate}]{.pre}: Sizes.

:   The [[matrix_handler]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler){.reference .internal}
    class manages matrix-based quantum operators. It derives from
    [[operator_handler]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1operator__handler){.reference .internal}
    and facilitates the definition, instantiation, evaluation, and
    manipulation of elementary as well as custom operators that can be
    represented in matrix form.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

                .notranslate}[`2}`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre}.

            -   **\`parameters\`** -- : A map specifying runtime
                parameter values. If the multi-diagonal matrix
                representation is not available, it will return empty.

    []{#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler_1abf23fc361c23942255099eded401fadf .target}[[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[[==]{.pre}]{.o}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[matrix_handler]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14matrix_handlerE "cudaq::matrix_handler"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[other]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq14matrix_handlereqERK14matrix_handler "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    []{#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler_1af43ec196f96d29a762a01b6972fb089f .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[void]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[define]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[operator_id]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[int64_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[expected_dimensions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[[matrix_callback]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15matrix_callbackE "cudaq::matrix_callback"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[create]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[parameter_descriptions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14matrix_handler6defineENSt6stringENSt6vectorINSt7int64_tEEERR15matrix_callbackRKNSt13unordered_mapINSt6stringENSt6stringEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Adds the definition of an elementary operator with the given id
        to the class. After definition, an the defined elementary
        operator can be instantiated by providing the operator id as
        well as the degree(s) of freedom that it acts on. An elementary
        operator is a parameterized object acting on certain degrees of
        freedom. To evaluate an operator, for example to compute its
        matrix, the level, that is the dimension, for each degree of
        freedom it acts on must be provided, as well as all additional
        parameters. Additional parameters must be provided in the form
        of keyword arguments. Note: The dimensions passed during
        operator evaluation are automatically validated against the
        expected dimensions specified during definition - the
        [`create`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} function does
        not need to do this.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   -   **operator_id** -- : A string that uniquely identifies
                the defined operator.

            -   **expected_dimensions** -- : Defines the number of
                levels, that is the dimension, for each degree of
                freedom in canonical (that is sorted) order. A negative
                or zero value for one (or more) of the expected
                dimensions indicates that the operator is defined for
                any dimension of the corresponding degree of freedom.

            -   **create** -- : Takes any number of complex-valued
                arguments and returns the matrix representing the
                operator. The matrix must be ordered such that the value
                returned by [`op.degrees()`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre} matches the order of the matrix,
                where [`op`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} is
                the instantiated the operator defined here. The
                [`create`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}
                function must take a vector of integers that specifies
                the "number of levels" (the dimension) for each degree
                of freedom that the operator acts on, and an unordered
                map from string to complex double that contains
                additional parameters the operator may use.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler_1a61e6d9943ee409c8b302493a5b6988da .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[void]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[define]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[operator_id]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[int64_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[expected_dimensions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[[matrix_callback]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15matrix_callbackE "cudaq::matrix_callback"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[create]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[[diag_matrix_callback]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq20diag_matrix_callbackE "cudaq::diag_matrix_callback"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[diag_create]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[parameter_descriptions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14matrix_handler6defineENSt6stringENSt6vectorINSt7int64_tEEERR15matrix_callbackRR20diag_matrix_callbackRKNSt13unordered_mapINSt6stringENSt6stringEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

[]{#classcudaq_1_1product__op .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[product_op]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   Represents an operator expression consisting of a product of
    elementary and scalar operators. Operator expressions cannot be used
    within quantum kernels, but they provide methods to convert them to
    data types that can.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1product__op_1a137c24e6fb8c6f0e0410753a8b795bab .target}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[[degrees]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq10product_op7degreesEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   The degrees of freedom that the operator acts on. The order of
        degrees is from smallest to largest and reflects the ordering of
        the matrix returned by [`to_matrix`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}. Specifically, the indices of a statevector
        with two qubits are {00, 01, 10, 11}. An ordering of degrees {0,
        1} then indicates that a state where the qubit with index 0
        equals 1 with probability 1 is given by the vector {0., 1., 0.,
        0.}.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1product__op_1a4739575d26dfea7daa29acf6f527ff72 .target}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[num_ops]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq10product_op7num_opsEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Return the number of operator terms that make up this product
        operator.

    :   The term id uniquely identifies the operators and targets
        (degrees) that they act on, but does not include information
        about the coefficient.

    :   Constructs a product operator from an existing product operator
        with a different type. This constructor enables the creation of
        a new [[product_op]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal}
        object when the HandlerTy is a [[matrix_handler]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler){.reference
        .internal}, provided that the type T is not the same as
        HandlerTy but is convertible to HandlerTy. It allows for proper
        handling of commutation behavior during the construction.

        Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **T** -- The type of the operand from which the new
            [[product_op]{.std
            .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal}
            is constructed.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   -   **other** -- The source [[product_op]{.std
                .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference
                .internal} instance from which to create this new
                object.

            -   **behavior** -- The commutation behavior to be used with
                the [[matrix_handler]{.std
                .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1matrix__handler){.reference
                .internal}.

    []{#classcudaq_1_1product__op_1ace16881180154a36664458d7036e2af2 .target}[[[product_op]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "cudaq::product_op"){.reference .internal}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[HandlerTy]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "cudaq::product_op::HandlerTy"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[[=]{.pre}]{.o}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[product_op]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "cudaq::product_op"){.reference .internal}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[T]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0_NSt11enable_if_tIXaantNSt7is_sameI1T9HandlerTyE5valueENSt16is_constructibleI9HandlerTy1TE5valueEEbEEEN5cudaq10product_opaSER10product_opI9HandlerTyERK10product_opI1TE "cudaq::product_op::operator=::T"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[other]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4I0_NSt11enable_if_tIXaantNSt7is_sameI1T9HandlerTyE5valueENSt16is_constructibleI9HandlerTy1TE5valueEEbEEEN5cudaq10product_opaSER10product_opI9HandlerTyERK10product_opI1TE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Templated assignment operator that enables assigning from a
        [[product_op]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal}
        with a different but convertible type. This operator is only
        enabled when the template parameter T is not the same as
        HandlerTy and is constructible as a HandlerTy. It allows for
        copying or converting a [[product_op]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal}
        instance of type T into one of type HandlerTy.

        Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **T** -- The type of the [[product_op]{.std
            .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal}
            to be assigned from, which must satisfy that it is not
            HandlerTy and is constructible as HandlerTy.


    []{#classcudaq_1_1product__op_1a28374c9fd9263bc989359cfb8672c9da .target}[[[complex_matrix]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14complex_matrixE "cudaq::complex_matrix"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[[to_matrix]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[int64_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[dimensions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}, [[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[complex]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[parameters]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}, [[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[invert_order]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[false]{.pre}]{.k}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq10product_op9to_matrixENSt13unordered_mapINSt6size_tENSt7int64_tEEERKNSt13unordered_mapINSt6stringENSt7complexIdEEEEb "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Return the matrix representation of the operator. By default,
        the matrix is ordered according to the convention (endianness)
        used in CUDA-Q, and the ordering returned by default by
        [`degrees`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   -   **\`dimensions\`** -- : A mapping that specifies the
                number of levels, that is, the dimension of each degree
                of freedom that the operator acts on. Example for two,
                2-level degrees of freedom: [`{0:2,`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}[`1:2}`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre}.

            -   **\`parameters\`** -- : A map of the parameter names to
                their concrete, complex values.

                -   [`invert_order`{.docutils .literal
                    .notranslate}]{.pre}: if set to true, the ordering
                    convention is reversed.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1product__op_1a1d36922cacdc68f70fa941bea2dd65df .target}[[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[[==]{.pre}]{.o}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[product_op]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "cudaq::product_op"){.reference .internal}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[HandlerTy]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq10product_opE "cudaq::product_op::HandlerTy"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[other]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq10product_opeqERK10product_opI9HandlerTyE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   True, if the other value is an sum_op\<HandlerTy\> with
        equivalent terms, and False otherwise. The equality takes into
        account that operator addition is commutative, as is the product
        of two operators if they act on different degrees of freedom.
        The equality comparison does *not* take commutation relations
        into account, and does not try to reorder terms
        [`blockwise`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}; it may
        hence evaluate to False, even if two operators in reality are
        the same. If the equality evaluates to True, on the other hand,
        the operators are guaranteed to represent the same
        transformation for all arguments.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    :   Return the matrix representation of the operator. By default,
        the matrix is ordered according to the convention (endianness)
        used in CUDA-Q, and the ordering returned by
        [`degrees`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}. See the
        documentation for [`degrees`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre} for more detail.

        -   [`dimensions`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} : A
            mapping that specifies the number of levels, that is, the
            dimension of each degree of freedom that the operator acts
            on. Example for two, 2-level degrees of freedom:
            [`{0:2,`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}[`1:2}`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre}.

        -   [`parameters`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} : A
            map of the parameter names to their concrete, complex
            values.

        -   [`invert_order`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}: if
            set to true, the ordering convention is reversed.

    :   Overloads the multiplication operator to multiply a scalar
        operator with a product operator. This function enables
        left-sided multiplication of a scalar operator (provided as an
        rvalue reference) with an existing product operator, producing a
        new product operator that encapsulates the resultant state.

        Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **T** -- The type parameter used within the product
            operator.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   -   **other** -- The scalar operator to be multiplied
                (rvalue reference).

            -   **self** -- The product operator to be multiplied.

        Returns[:]{.colon}

        :   A new product operator that is the result of multiplying the
            scalar operator with the product operator.

        []{#structcudaq_1_1product__op_1_1const__iterator_1a51f584b8304d780d030c4db0b8563cca .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[[==]{.pre}]{.o}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[const_iterator]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq10product_op14const_iteratorE "cudaq::product_op::const_iterator"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[other]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq10product_op14const_iteratoreqERK14const_iterator "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

[[template]{.pre}]{.k}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[HandlerTy]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}\
[]{#classcudaq_1_1sum__op .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[sum_op]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq6sum_opE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   Represents a sum of operator products in a quantum operator algebra.

    The [[sum_op]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1sum__op){.reference
    .internal} class is a templated container that encapsulates a linear
    combination of product operators, where each term is defined by a
    specific configuration of operator components paired with a scalar
    coefficient.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1sum__op_1a6d5dd88ba7c6e4deb7e6660d2aeec7fc .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[const_iterator]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6sum_op14const_iteratorE "cudaq::sum_op::const_iterator"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[[begin]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq6sum_op5beginEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Get iterator to beginning of operator terms.


    :   Operator to get the product term at a particular index.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1sum__op_1a2206e037535e1f87a883a375a71f536e .target}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[[degrees]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq6sum_op7degreesEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   The degrees of freedom that the operator acts on. The order of
        degrees is from smallest to largest and reflect the ordering of
        the matrix returned by [`to_matrix`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}. Specifically, the indices of a statevector
        with two qubits are {00, 01, 10, 11}. An ordering of degrees {0,
        1} then indicates that a state where the qubit with index 0
        equals 1 with probability 1 is given by the vector {0., 1., 0.,
        0.}.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    :   Assigns a [[product_op]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1product__op){.reference .internal} to
        a [[sum_op]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1sum__op){.reference
        .internal}. This operator overload enables assignment from a
        product_op\<T\> to a sum_op\<HandlerTy\>. It is only enabled
        when T is not the same as HandlerTy and when HandlerTy is
        constructible from T. This constraint ensures that only
        compatible types are allowed in the assignment operation.

    []{#classcudaq_1_1sum__op_1ae671bd18e225e7aca97d66fffd7f266f .target}[[[complex_matrix]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14complex_matrixE "cudaq::complex_matrix"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[[to_matrix]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[int64_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[dimensions]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}, [[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[unordered_map]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[complex]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[parameters]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[{]{.pre}]{.p}[[}]{.pre}]{.p}, [[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[invert_order]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[false]{.pre}]{.k}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq6sum_op9to_matrixENSt13unordered_mapINSt6size_tENSt7int64_tEEERKNSt13unordered_mapINSt6stringENSt7complexIdEEEEb "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Return the matrix representation of the operator. By default,
        the matrix is ordered according to the convention (endianness)
        used in CUDA-Q, and the ordering returned by default by
        [`degrees`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   -   **\`dimensions\`** -- : A mapping that specifies the
                number of levels, that is, the dimension of each degree
                of freedom that the operator acts on. Example for two,
                2-level degrees of freedom: [`{0:2,`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}[`1:2}`{.docutils .literal
                .notranslate}]{.pre}.

            -   **\`parameters\`** -- : A map of the parameter names to
                their concrete, complex values.

                -   [`invert_order`{.docutils .literal
                    .notranslate}]{.pre}: if set to true, the ordering
                    convention is reversed.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1sum__op_1af34bb59f34cb4f7ac491144d8f6e890e .target}[[bool]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[[==]{.pre}]{.o}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[sum_op]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq6sum_opE "cudaq::sum_op"){.reference .internal}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[HandlerTy]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq6sum_opE "cudaq::sum_op::HandlerTy"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[other]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4NK5cudaq6sum_opeqERK6sum_opI9HandlerTyE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   True, if the other value is an sum_op\<HandlerTy\> with
        equivalent terms, and False otherwise. The equality takes into
        account that operator addition is commutative, as is the product
        of two operators if they act on different degrees of freedom.
        The equality comparison does *not* take commutation relations
        into account, and does not try to reorder terms
        [`blockwise`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}; it may
        hence evaluate to False, even if two operators in reality are
        the same. If the equality evaluates to True, on the other hand,
        the operators are guaranteed to represent the same
        transformation for all arguments.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    :   Return the matrix representation of the operator. By default,
        the matrix is ordered according to the convention (endianness)
        used in CUDA-Q, and the ordering returned by
        [`degrees`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}. See the
        documentation for [`degrees`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre} for more detail.

        -   [`dimensions`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} : A
            mapping that specifies the number of levels, that is, the
            dimension of each degree of freedom that the operator acts
            on. Example for two, 2-level degrees of freedom:
            [`{0:2,`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}[`1:2}`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre}.

        -   [`parameters`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} : A
            map of the parameter names to their concrete, complex
            values.

        -   [`invert_order`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}: if
            set to true, the ordering convention is reversed.


    :   Return the multi-diagonal matrix representation of the operator.
        By default, the matrix is ordered according to the convention
        (endianness) used in CUDA-Q, and the ordering returned by
        [`degrees`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}. See the
        documentation for [`degrees`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre} for more detail.

            mapping that specifies the number of levels, that is, the
            dimension of each degree of freedom that the operator acts
            on. Example for two, 2-level degrees of freedom:
            [`{0:2,`{.docutils .literal

            .notranslate}[`1:2}`{.docutils .literal
            .notranslate}]{.pre}.

[]{#classcudaq_1_1qreg .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[qreg]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4I_NSt6size_tE_NSt6size_tE0EN5cudaq4qregE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A [`qreg`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} is a container for
    qudits. This container can be dynamic or compile-time-size
    specified. By default, the [`qreg`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre} is constructed as a dynamic register
    (vector-like) of qubits (2-level). This can be changed via the
    [`qreg`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} type template
    parameters.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Types

[]{#classcudaq_1_1qvector .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[qvector]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4I_NSt6size_tEEN5cudaq7qvectorE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A [`qvector`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} is an owning,
    dynamically sized container for qudits. The semantics of the
    [`qvector`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} follows that of a
    [`std::vector`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} for qudits.
    It is templated on the number of levels for the held qudits.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

## Common[](#common "Permalink to this heading"){.headerlink}

[]{#classcudaq_1_1observe__result .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[observe_result]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14observe_resultE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[observe_result]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1observe__result){.reference .internal}
    encapsulates all data generated from a cudaq"::"observe call. This
    includes all measurement counts from the execution of each ansatz +
    measure circuit, and the global expected value of the spin_op passed
    to observe.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1observe__result_1aba859a67c28ee73dee0943043de4b419 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[observe_result]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[e]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[spin_op]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq7spin_opE "cudaq::spin_op"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[H]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14observe_result14observe_resultEdRK7spin_op "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Constructor, takes the precomputed expectation value for
        \<psi(x) \| H \| psi(x)\> for the given spin_op.

    []{#classcudaq_1_1observe__result_1aa3bb86339bb588bdc812ae27c9e8eb8a .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[operator]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14observe_resultcvdEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Conversion operator for this [[[`observe_result`{.docutils
        .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1observe__result){.reference .internal}
        to [`double`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}. Simply
        returns the precomputed expectation value for the given spin_op.
        This enables one to ignore the fine-grain [[sample_result]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1sample__result){.reference .internal}
        data, and explicitly request the expected value: double exp =
        cudaq"::"observe(...); as opposed to cudaq"::"observe_data data
        = cudaq::observe(...); auto exp = data.expectation();.


[]{#structcudaq_1_1observe__options .target}[[struct]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[observe_options]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15observe_optionsE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   Observe options to provide as an argument to the
    [`observe()`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre},
    [`async_observe()`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}
    functions.

    Param shots[:]{.colon}

    :   number of shots to run for the given kernel, or -1 if not
        applicable.

    Param noise[:]{.colon}

    :   noise model to use for the sample operation

    Param num_trajectories[:]{.colon}

    :   is the optional number of trajectories to be used when computing
        the expectation values in the presence of noise. This parameter
        is only applied to simulation backends that support noisy
        simulation of trajectories.

        mechanism ID is independent of all other error mechanism ID. For
        all errors with the *same* ID, only one of them can happen. That

        other.

[]{#classcudaq_1_1details_1_1future .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[future]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq7details6futureE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The future type models the expected result of a CUDA-Q kernel
    execution under a specific execution context. This type is returned
    from asynchronous execution calls. It encapsulates the job-specific
    circuit execution identifiers, the name of the [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} the job
    executed on, and any extra configuration information needed to
    retrieve the results later from the server. This type can be
    persisted to file and read in later to retrieve execution results.
    It also optionally wraps a std::future\<T\> type, and in this case,
    persistence to file is not allowed, .get() must be invoked at some
    later point within the same runtime context.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1details_1_1future_1a8a3afaa7207cba1092a88568d2bc2d14 .target}[[[future]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[default]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq7details6future6futureEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   The constructor.

:   the [[async_result]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1async__result){.reference .internal} type
    is a user facing, future-like type that is returned from CUDA-Q
    public asynchronous API functions. It wraps a
    [[details::future]{.std

    type, which can itself be constructed from a std::future or a
    collection of data pertinent to remote [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} REST
    invocation.

[]{#structcudaq_1_1ExecutionResult .target}[[struct]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[ExecutionResult]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15ExecutionResultE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[[`ExecutionResult`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#structcudaq_1_1ExecutionResult){.reference .internal}
    models the result of a typical quantum state sampling task. It will
    contain the observed measurement bit strings and corresponding
    number of times observed, as well as an expected value with respect
    to the Z...Z operator.

[]{#classcudaq_1_1sample__result .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[sample_result]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13sample_resultE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[sample_result]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1sample__result){.reference .internal}
    abstraction wraps a set of [[[`ExecutionResult`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#structcudaq_1_1ExecutionResult){.reference .internal}s
    for a single quantum kernel execution under the sampling or
    observation [[[`ExecutionContext`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1ExecutionContext){.reference .internal}.
    Each [[[`ExecutionResult`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#structcudaq_1_1ExecutionResult){.reference .internal} is
    mapped to a register name, with a default
    [[[`ExecutionResult`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#structcudaq_1_1ExecutionResult){.reference .internal}
    with name **global** representing the observed measurement results
    holistically for the quantum kernel.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1sample__result_1ae8f611495ea923027a4008a4da8019a8 .target}[[[sample_result]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[default]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13sample_result13sample_resultEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Nullary constructor.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

:   Sample the given quantum kernel expression and return the mapping of
    observed bit strings to corresponding number of times observed.

    Given a quantum kernel with void return type, sample the

    returning the mapping of bits observed to number of times it was
    observed.

    :   -   **options** -- Sample options.

        -   **kernel** -- The kernel expression, must contain final
            measurements.

        -   **args** -- The variadic concrete arguments for evaluation
            of the kernel.

:   Sample the given quantum kernel expression and return the mapping of
    observed bit strings to corresponding number of times observed.
    Specify the number of shots.

    This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It
    differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

    Given a quantum kernel with void return type, sample the

    returning the mapping of bits observed to number of times it was
    observed.

            of the kernel.

[]{#classcudaq_1_1SimulationState .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[SimulationState]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15SimulationStateE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[[`SimulationState`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1SimulationState){.reference .internal}
    interface provides and extension point for concrete circuit
    simulation sub-types to describe their underlying quantum state data
    in an efficient manner. The [[[`SimulationState`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1SimulationState){.reference .internal}
    provides a handle on the data for clients, with data remaining on
    GPU device or CPU memory. The primary goal of this type and its
    sub-types is to minimize data transfers for the state.

    Subclassed by [[cudaq::CusvState\< ScalarType \>]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1CusvState){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::QPUState]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPUState){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::RemoteSimulationState]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1RemoteSimulationState){.reference
    .internal}, [[nvqir::MPSSimulationState\< ScalarType \>]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classnvqir_1_1MPSSimulationState){.reference .internal},
    [[nvqir::TensorNetSimulationState\< ScalarType \>]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classnvqir_1_1TensorNetSimulationState){.reference
    .internal}

```{=html}
<!-- -->
```

[[template]{.pre}]{.k}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[ScalarType]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}\
[]{#classcudaq_1_1CusvState .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[CusvState]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[SimulationState]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15SimulationStateE "cudaq::SimulationState"){.reference .internal}[](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq9CusvStateE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   [[CusvState]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1CusvState){.reference
    .internal} provides an implementation of
    [[[`SimulationState`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1SimulationState){.reference .internal}
    that encapsulates the state data for the Custatevec Circuit
    Simulator. It attempts to keep the simulation data on GPU device and
    care is taken to ensure operations and comparisons with other states
    operate on compatible floating point element types.


[]{#classcudaq_1_1Trace .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[Trace]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq5TraceE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A trace is a circuit representation of the executed computation, as
    seen by the execution manager. (Here, a circuit is represented as a
    list of instructions on qudits). Since the execution manager cannot
    "see" control flow, the trace of a kernel with control flow
    represents a single execution path, and thus two calls to the same
    kernel might produce traces.

```{=html}
<!-- -->
```

    (exclusive).

[]{#classcudaq_1_1Resources .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[Resources]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq9ResourcesE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[Resources]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1Resources){.reference .internal} type
    encodes information regarding the currently executing kernel's
    resource usage. This includes number and type of quantum operation,
    circuit depth, etc.


[]{#classcudaq_1_1complex__matrix_1ade050d2b1512d2fe61d2f69810419bc4 .target}[[using]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[complex_matrix]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14complex_matrixE "cudaq::complex_matrix"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}]{.sig-prename .descclassname}[[[value_type]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[complex]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14complex_matrix10value_typeE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

::: {#noise-modeling .section}
## Noise Modeling[](#noise-modeling "Permalink to this heading"){.headerlink}

[[template]{.pre}]{.k}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[Channel]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[\...]{.pre}]{.p}[[[Args]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}\
[[void]{.pre}]{.kt}[ ]{.w}[[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}]{.sig-prename .descclassname}[[[apply_noise]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[[Args]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0DpEN5cudaq11apply_noiseEvDpRR4Args "cudaq::apply_noise::Args"){.reference .internal}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[\...]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[args]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4I0DpEN5cudaq11apply_noiseEvDpRR4Args "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   This function is a type-safe injection of noise into a quantum
    kernel, occurring precisely at the call site of the function
    invocation. The function should be called inside CUDA-Q kernels
    (those annotated with [`__qpu__`{.code .docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}). The functionality is only supported for
    simulation targets, so it is automatically (and silently) stripped
    from any programs submitted to hardware targets.

    Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

    :   **Channel** --

        A subtype of [[`cudaq::kraus_channel`{.xref .cpp .cpp-class
        .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "cudaq::kraus_channel"){.reference
        .internal} that implements/defines the desired noise mechanisms
        as Kraus channels (e.g. [[`cudaq::depolarization2`{.xref .cpp
        .cpp-class .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15depolarization2E "cudaq::depolarization2"){.reference
        .internal}). If you want to use a custom
        [[`cudaq::kraus_channel`{.xref .cpp .cpp-class .docutils
        .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "cudaq::kraus_channel"){.reference
        .internal} (i.e. not built-in to CUDA-Q), it must first be
        registered *outside the kernel* with
        [[`cudaq::noise_model::register_channel()`{.xref .cpp .cpp-func
        .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}](#_CPPv4I00EN5cudaq11noise_model16register_channelEvv "cudaq::noise_model::register_channel"){.reference
        .internal}, like this:

        ::: {.highlight-cpp .notranslate}
        ::: highlight
            struct my_custom_kraus_channel_subtype : public ::cudaq::kraus_channel {
              static constexpr std::size_t num_parameters = 1;
              static constexpr std::size_t num_targets = 1;

              my_custom_kraus_channel_subtype(const std::vector<cudaq::real> &params) {
                  std::vector<cudaq::complex> k0v{std::sqrt(1 - params[0]), 0, 0,
                                                  std::sqrt(1 - params[0])},
                      k1v{0, std::sqrt(params[0]), std::sqrt(params[0]), 0};
                  push_back(cudaq::kraus_op(k0v));
                  push_back(cudaq::kraus_op(k1v));
                  validateCompleteness();
                  generateUnitaryParameters();
              }
              REGISTER_KRAUS_CHANNEL("my_custom_kraus_channel_subtype");
            };

            cudaq::noise_model noise;
            noise.register_channel<my_custom_kraus_channel_subtype>();
        :::
        :::

    Parameters[:]{.colon}

    :   **args** --

        The precise argument pack depend on the concrete
        [`Channel`{.code .docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre} being
        used. The arguments are a concatenated list of parameters and
        targets. For example, to apply a 2-qubit depolarization channel,
        which has [`num_parameters`{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}[`=`{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}[`1`{.code .docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}
        and [`num_targets`{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}[`=`{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}` `{.code .docutils .literal
        .notranslate}[`2`{.code .docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre},
        one would write the call like this:

        ::: {.highlight-cpp .notranslate}
        ::: highlight
            cudaq::qubit q, r;
            cudaq::apply_noise<cudaq::depolarization2>(/*probability=*/0.1, q, r);
        :::
        :::


[]{#structcudaq_1_1kraus__op .target}[[struct]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[kraus_op]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq8kraus_opE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A [[kraus_op]{.std .std-ref}](#structcudaq_1_1kraus__op){.reference
    .internal} represents a single Kraus operation, described as a
    complex matrix of specific size. The matrix is represented here as a
    1d array (specifically a std::vector).

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}


[]{#classcudaq_1_1kraus__channel .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[kraus_channel]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A [[kraus_channel]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1kraus__channel){.reference .internal}
    represents a quantum noise channel on specific qubits. The action of
    the noise channel is described by a vector of Kraus operations -
    matrices with size equal to 2\*\*nQubits x 2\*\*nQubits, where the
    number of qubits is the number of provided qubit indices at
    construction.

    Subclassed by [[cudaq::amplitude_damping_channel]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1amplitude__damping__channel){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::bit_flip_channel]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1bit__flip__channel){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::depolarization2]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1depolarization2){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::depolarization_channel]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1depolarization__channel){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::pauli1]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1pauli1){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::pauli2]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1pauli2){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::phase_damping]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1phase__damping){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::phase_flip_channel]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1phase__flip__channel){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::y_error]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1y__error){.reference .internal}

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

[]{#classcudaq_1_1pauli1 .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[pauli1]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[kraus_channel]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "cudaq::kraus_channel"){.reference .internal}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli1E "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A single-qubit Pauli error that applies either an X error, Y error,
    or Z error, with 3 probabilities specified as inputs.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1pauli1_1aa44116b940f9aa114491bcff1e858277 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[pauli1]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[real]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq4realE "cudaq::real"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[p]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli16pauli1ERKNSt6vectorIN5cudaq4realEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Construct a single-qubit Pauli error Kraus channel.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **p** -- Error probabilities for X, Y, and Z errors,
            respectively
    :::

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Static Attributes

    []{#classcudaq_1_1pauli1_1aaa6c40117ffc5e446518fe6863bb8042 .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[constexpr]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[num_parameters]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[3]{.pre}]{.m}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli114num_parametersE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Number of parameters. The 3 parameters are the probability that
        an X error, Y error, or Z error happens. Only 1 of the 3
        possible errors will happen (at most).


[]{#classcudaq_1_1pauli2 .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[pauli2]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[kraus_channel]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "cudaq::kraus_channel"){.reference .internal}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli2E "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A 2-qubit Pauli error that applies one of the following errors, with
    the probabilities specified as inputs. Possible errors: IX, IY, IZ,
    XI, XX, XY, XZ, YI, YX, YY, YZ, ZI, ZX, ZY, and ZZ.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1pauli2_1a0872eff8b7aad135aabf2fc8de8cd8e3 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[pauli2]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[real]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq4realE "cudaq::real"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[p]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli26pauli2ERKNSt6vectorIN5cudaq4realEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Construct a 2-qubit Pauli error Kraus channel.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **p** -- Error probabilities for the 2-qubit Pauli
            operators. The length of this vector must be 15. Note that
            since the probability of II is not specified, it is implied
            to by 1 - sum(p). Therefore, maximal mixing occurs when
            sum(p) = 0.9375.
    :::

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Static Attributes

    []{#classcudaq_1_1pauli2_1a09a6184772a27fd4385606619b1ec011 .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[constexpr]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[num_parameters]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[15]{.pre}]{.m}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli214num_parametersE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Number of parameters. The 15 parameters are the probability that
        each one of the above errors will happen. Only 1 of the 15
        possible errors will happen (at most).

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1pauli2_1aac5380625e186042a8ced4ed49409658 .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[constexpr]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[num_targets]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[2]{.pre}]{.m}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq6pauli211num_targetsE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :::

[]{#classcudaq_1_1depolarization2 .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[depolarization2]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[kraus_channel]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq13kraus_channelE "cudaq::kraus_channel"){.reference .internal}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15depolarization2E "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A 2-qubit depolarization error that applies one of the following
    errors. Possible errors: IX, IY, IZ, XI, XX, XY, XZ, YI, YX, YY, YZ,
    ZI, ZX, ZY, and ZZ.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1depolarization2_1aa0a6744f70184f41dc6218cebb886d07 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[depolarization2]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[const]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[real]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq4realE "cudaq::real"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[probability]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15depolarization215depolarization2EK4real "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Construct a two qubit Kraus channel that applies a
        depolarization channel on either qubit independently.

        Parameters[:]{.colon}

        :   **probability** -- The probability of any depolarizing error
            happening in the 2 qubits. (Setting this to 1.0 ensures that
            "II" cannot happen; maximal mixing occurs at p = 0.9375.)
    :::

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Static Attributes

    []{#classcudaq_1_1depolarization2_1a7e554ebbab167ebf683771b4537091a9 .target}[[static]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[constexpr]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[size_t]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[num_parameters]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[1]{.pre}]{.m}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq15depolarization214num_parametersE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Number of parameters. The 1 parameter is the probability that
        each one of the 15 error possibilities list above will occur.
        Only 1 of the 15 possible errors will happen (at most).


[]{#classcudaq_1_1noise__model .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[noise_model]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq11noise_modelE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[noise_model]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1noise__model){.reference .internal} type
    keeps track of a set of kraus_channels to be applied after the
    execution of quantum operations. Each quantum operation maps to a
    Kraus channel containing a number of kraus_ops to be applied to the
    density matrix representation of the state.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Types

    []{#classcudaq_1_1kernel__builder_1a1823a80e0f41cab9edcd403d39c3e219 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[QuakeValue]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq10QuakeValueE "cudaq::QuakeValue"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[[qalloc]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[complex]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[state]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq14kernel_builder6qallocERNSt6vectorINSt7complexIdEEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Return a [[[`QuakeValue`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QuakeValue){.reference .internal}
        representing the allocated quantum register, initialized to the
        given state vector, [`state`{.docutils .literal
        .notranslate}]{.pre}.

        Note: input argument is a *true* reference here, the calling
        context has to own the data. Specifically, the builder object
        will capture variables by reference (implemented as a container
        of pointers for simplicity) but the builder does not create,
        own, or copy these vectors. This implies that if the captured
        vector goes out of scope before the kernel is invoked, the
        reference may contain garbage. This behavior is identical to a
        C++ lambda capture by reference.

```{=html}
<!-- -->
```

[]{#classcudaq_1_1QuakeValue .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[QuakeValue]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq10QuakeValueE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A [[QuakeValue]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QuakeValue){.reference .internal} is meant
    to provide a thin wrapper around an mlir::Value instance. These
    QuakeValues represent handles to function arguments and return
    values from MLIR Operations, specifically Quake Dialect operations.
    The [[QuakeValue]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QuakeValue){.reference .internal} also
    exposes and algebraic API enabling one to negate, add, subtract, and
    multiply QuakeValues with each other as well as with primitive
    arithmetic types, e.g. double.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

[]{#classcudaq_1_1details_1_1KernelBuilderType .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[KernelBuilderType]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq7details17KernelBuilderTypeE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [`kernel_builder::Type`{.docutils .literal .notranslate}]{.pre}
    allows us to track input C++ types representing the quake function
    argument types in a way that does not expose MLIR Type to the CUDA-Q
    code. This type keeps track of a functor that generates the MLIR
    Type in implementation code when [[create()]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1details_1_1KernelBuilderType_1ae62efe009d225bfc935230fd0d74fca7){.reference
    .internal} is invoked.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

::: {#algorithms .section}
## Algorithms[](#algorithms "Permalink to this heading"){.headerlink}

[]{#classcudaq_1_1optimizer .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[optimizer]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq9optimizerE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[cudaq::optimizer]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1optimizer){.reference .internal} provides
    a high-level interface for general optimization of user-specified
    objective functions. This is meant to serve an interface for clients
    working with concrete subtypes providing specific optimization
    algorithms possibly delegating to third party libraries. This
    interface provides an optimize(...) method that takes the number of
    objective function input parameters (the dimension), and a
    user-specified objective function that takes the function input
    parameters as a immutable ([`const`{.docutils .literal
    .notranslate}]{.pre}) vector\<double\> reference and a mutable
    vector\<double\> reference modeling the current iteration gradient
    vector (dF / dx_i, for all i parameters). This function must return
    a scalar double, the value of this function at the current input
    parameters. The optimizer also exposes a method for querying whether
    the current optimization strategy requires gradients or not.
    Parameterizing optimization strategies is left as a task for
    sub-types (things like initial parameters, max function evaluations,
    etc.).

    ::: {.highlight-cpp .notranslate}
    ::: highlight
        cudaq::optimizers::cobyla opt;
        assert(!opt.requiresGradients() && "Cobyla algo does not use gradients.");
        auto [opt_val, opt_params] = opt.optimize(2,
                      [&](const std::vector<double>& x, std::vector<double>& dx) {
                          ... use x, modify dx, return scalar double ...
                      }
                    );
    :::
    :::

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}

[]{#classcudaq_1_1gradient .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[gradient]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq8gradientE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[cudaq::gradient]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradient){.reference .internal} represents
    a base type for all gradient strategies leveraged by variational
    algorithms.

    The [[cudaq::gradient]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradient){.reference .internal} tracks a
    std::function with signature void(std::vector\<double\>)
    representing the parameterized kernel ansatz. For ansatzes that do
    not follow this signature, a separate Argument Mapper must be
    provided which takes std::vector\<double\> to a tuple of custom
    function arguments. All gradient subtypes should inherit the base
    class constructors (using gradient::gradient), but provide a
    concrete implementation of [[gradient::compute()]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradient_1a00ec8d88812a7d459ee134e4b5c9593c){.reference
    .internal}. The compute method takes as input the current iteration
    parameters, a reference to the gradient vector which
    [[compute()]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradient_1a00ec8d88812a7d459ee134e4b5c9593c){.reference
    .internal} must update, the cudaq::spin_op for this variational
    algorithm, and the expected value of the spin_op at the current
    iteration's parameters. Subtypes can leverage the protected
    gradient::getExpectedValue() method to compute \<psi(x) \| H \|
    psi(x)\> at the provided set of variational parameters.

    Subclassed by [[cudaq::gradients::central_difference]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradients_1_1central__difference){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::gradients::forward_difference]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradients_1_1forward__difference){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::gradients::parameter_shift]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1gradients_1_1parameter__shift){.reference
    .internal}

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

    []{#classcudaq_1_1gradient_1ab284b63287df8a9c5f30a10c472e77eb .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[gradient]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[function]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[void]{.pre}]{.kt}[[(]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[vector]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[double]{.pre}]{.kt}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[)]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[kernel]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq8gradient8gradientERRNSt8functionIFvNSt6vectorIdEEEEE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Constructor, takes the quantum kernel with prescribed signature.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    []{#classcudaq_1_1gradient_1acc76a46b709b332d3475ce585abf2e99 .target}[[[gradient]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[)]{.sig-paren}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[default]{.pre}]{.k}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq8gradient8gradientEv "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Empty constructor.

    ```{=html}
    <!-- -->
    ```

    [[template]{.pre}]{.k}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[KernelT]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[ArgsMapper]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}\
    []{#classcudaq_1_1gradient_1adcc5f751cb413adec4a5baccd652a4d9 .target}[[inline]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[gradient]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[[KernelT]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I00EN5cudaq8gradient8gradientER7KernelTRR10ArgsMapper "cudaq::gradient::gradient::KernelT"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[kernel]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[[ArgsMapper]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I00EN5cudaq8gradient8gradientER7KernelTRR10ArgsMapper "cudaq::gradient::gradient::ArgsMapper"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[argsMapper]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4I00EN5cudaq8gradient8gradientER7KernelTRR10ArgsMapper "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

    :   Constructor, takes a callable with non-standard signature the
        Argument Mapper function object that maps the parameters to
        concrete arguments for the quantum kernel.


## Platform[](#platform "Permalink to this heading"){.headerlink}

[]{#classcudaq_1_1QPU .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[QPU]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[registry]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq8registryE "cudaq::registry"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[RegisteredType]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0EN5cudaq8registry14RegisteredTypeE "cudaq::registry::RegisteredType"){.reference .internal}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[QPU]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq3QPUE "cudaq::QPU"){.reference .internal}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq3QPUE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   A CUDA-Q [[QPU]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference
    .internal} is an abstraction on the quantum processing unit which
    executes quantum kernel expressions. The [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} exposes certain
    information about the [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} being
    targeting, such as the number of available qubits, the logical ID
    for this [[QPU]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference
    .internal} in a set of available QPUs, and its qubit connectivity.
    The [[QPU]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal}
    keeps track of an execution queue for enqueuing asynchronous tasks
    that execute quantum kernel expressions. The [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} also tracks the
    client-provided execution context to enable quantum kernel related
    tasks such as sampling and observation.

    This type is meant to be subtyped by concrete
    [[quantum_platform]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1quantum__platform){.reference .internal}
    subtypes.

    Subclassed by [[cudaq::BaseRemoteRESTQPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1BaseRemoteRESTQPU){.reference .internal},
    [[cudaq::BaseRemoteSimulatorQPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1BaseRemoteSimulatorQPU){.reference
    .internal}, [[cudaq::OrcaRemoteRESTQPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1OrcaRemoteRESTQPU){.reference .internal}

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions


[]{#classcudaq_1_1OrcaRemoteRESTQPU .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[OrcaRemoteRESTQPU]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[ ]{.w}[[:]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[public]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[QPU]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq3QPUE "cudaq::QPU"){.reference .internal}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq17OrcaRemoteRESTQPUE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[OrcaRemoteRESTQPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1OrcaRemoteRESTQPU){.reference .internal}
    is a subtype of [[QPU]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference .internal} that enables
    the execution of CUDA-Q kernels on remotely hosted quantum computing
    services via a REST Client / Server interaction. This type is meant
    to be general enough to support any remotely hosted service.
    Moreover, this [[QPU]{.std .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1QPU){.reference
    .internal} handles launching kernels under the Execution Context
    that includes sampling via synchronous client invocations.

```{=html}

```

[]{#classcudaq_1_1quantum__platform .target}[[class]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[quantum_platform]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[](#_CPPv4N5cudaq16quantum_platformE "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   The [[quantum_platform]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1quantum__platform){.reference .internal}
    corresponds to a specific quantum architecture. The
    [[quantum_platform]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1quantum__platform){.reference .internal}
    exposes a public API for programmers to query specific information
    about the targeted QPU(s) (e.g. number of qubits, qubit
    connectivity, etc.). This type is meant to be subclassed for
    concrete realizations of quantum platforms, which are intended to
    populate this platformQPUs member of this base class.

    ::: {.breathe-sectiondef .docutils .container}
    Public Functions

[[template]{.pre}]{.k}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[[QuantumKernel]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[\...]{.pre}]{.p}[[[Args]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[typename]{.pre}]{.k}[ ]{.w}[[=]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[enable_if_t]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[is_invocable_v]{.pre}]{.n}[[\<]{.pre}]{.p}[[[QuantumKernel]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0Dp0EN5cudaq7contrib4drawENSt6stringERR13QuantumKernelDpRR4Args "cudaq::contrib::draw::QuantumKernel"){.reference .internal}[[,]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[[Args]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0Dp0EN5cudaq7contrib4drawENSt6stringERR13QuantumKernelDpRR4Args "cudaq::contrib::draw::Args"){.reference .internal}[[\...]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}[[\>]{.pre}]{.p}\
[]{#draw_8h_1a5ba1c68731156efd49a310a05362e3e5 .target}[[std]{.pre}]{.n}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[string]{.pre}]{.n}[ ]{.w}[[[[cudaq]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv45cudaq "cudaq"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}[[[contrib]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4N5cudaq7contribE "cudaq::contrib"){.reference .internal}[[::]{.pre}]{.p}]{.sig-prename .descclassname}[[[draw]{.pre}]{.n}]{.sig-name .descname}[(]{.sig-paren}[[[QuantumKernel]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0Dp0EN5cudaq7contrib4drawENSt6stringERR13QuantumKernelDpRR4Args "cudaq::contrib::draw::QuantumKernel"){.reference .internal}[ ]{.w}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[kernel]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}, [[[Args]{.pre}]{.n}](#_CPPv4I0Dp0EN5cudaq7contrib4drawENSt6stringERR13QuantumKernelDpRR4Args "cudaq::contrib::draw::Args"){.reference .internal}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[&]{.pre}]{.p}[[\...]{.pre}]{.p}[ ]{.w}[[args]{.pre}]{.n .sig-param}[)]{.sig-paren}[](#_CPPv4I0Dp0EN5cudaq7contrib4drawENSt6stringERR13QuantumKernelDpRR4Args "Permalink to this definition"){.headerlink}\

:   Returns a drawing of the execution path, i.e., the trace, of the
    kernel. The drawing is a UTF-8 encoded string.

    Usage:

    ::: {.highlight-cpp .notranslate}
    ::: highlight
        #include <cudaq.h>
        #include <cudaq/algorithms/draw.h>
        #include <iostream>

        auto bell_pair = []() __qpu__ {
            cudaq::qvector q(2);
            h(q[0]);
            x<cudaq::ctrl>(q[0], q[1]);
            mz(q);
        };
        ...
        std::cout << cudaq::contrib::draw(bell_pair);
        /* Output:
                  
        q0 :  h 
             
        q1 :  x 
                  
        */

        auto kernel = [](float angle) __qpu__ {
          cudaq::qvector q(1);
          h(q[0]);
          ry(angle, q[0]);
        };
        ...
        std::cout << cudaq::contrib::draw(kernel, 0.59);
        /* Output:
             
        q0 :  h  ry(0.59) 
             
        */      
    :::
    :::

    Parameters[:]{.colon}

    :   -   **kernel** -- The quantum callable with non-trivial function
            signature.

        -   **args** -- The arguments required for evaluation of the
            quantum kernel.

    Returns[:]{.colon}

    :   The UTF-8 encoded string of the circuit, without measurement
        operations.

```{=html}
<!-- -->
```

:   Execute a quantum kernel and return its unitary as a
    [[complex_matrix]{.std
    .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1complex__matrix){.reference .internal}.

    Template Parameters[:]{.colon}

    :   **QuantumKernel** -- The functor type of the quantum kernel.

    Parameters[:]{.colon}

    :   -   **kernel** -- The quantum kernel to execute.

        -   **args** -- Arguments to pass to the kernel.

    Returns[:]{.colon}

    :   The full system unitary as a [[complex_matrix]{.std
        .std-ref}](#classcudaq_1_1complex__matrix){.reference
        .internal}.
